Well Evaluation
Marathon Oil Company
Angela Ward USA 24-7H
Figure 1. H&P rig 386 drilling the Marathon Oil Company,
Angela Ward USA 24-7H in Dunn County, North Dakota in November of 2014
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company, Angela Ward USA 24-7H [Lot 1 Section 18 , T146N, R92W; 771'
FNL & 1,115' FWL] is located approximately 8.5 miles north and 7 miles east of the town of
Dunn Center in Dunn County, North Dakota (Figure 1). The Angela Ward USA 24-7H will be a
dual section well, with an approximately 10,000' long lateral designed to further oil production
in the area. The surface will be drilled using freshwater drilling fluid, while the vertical and
curve sections will use diesel invert drilling fluid. Well plans called for the vertical section to be
drilled to a kick off point of 9,521' measured depth (MD). The curve would then be built at a rate
of 12.00º/100', and land in the middle of the Middle Bakken Member, target interval set by the
Marathon Oil Company geologist. After casing the vertical and curve, the lateral will be drilled
using salt-water drilling fluid. Geo-steering and directional drilling techniques will be used to
maintain maximum exposure to the target zone. The planned lateral section was to be drilled
north at an azimuth of 4.46°. Upon anticipated completion of the well, the hole will be prepared
for casing and production evaluation.
OFFSET WELLS
Three offset wells were used as primary controls while drilling the Angela Ward USA 24-7H.
Data including gamma-ray signatures and electric logs from nearby offset wells were used to
determine a prognosis of formation tops. These wells include:
The Dellana Ward USA 14-7H [Lot 1 Section 18, T146N, R92W] which is located
approximately 100 feet west of the Angela Ward USA 24-7H. This well was drilled
by Marathon Oil Company in September of 2014. It is a lateral, Middle Bakken
well and is currently awaiting completion.
The Roehr USA 34-7H [SE NW Section 18, T146N, R92W] which is located
approximately 2,590' southeast of the Angela Ward USA 24-7H. This well was
drilled by Marathon Oil Company. It is a lateral, Middle Bakken well and is
currently active.
The FLB-Askew [SE SE Section 14, T146N, R93W] which is located
approximately 9,150' southwest of the Angela Ward USA 24-7H. This well was
drilled by ANR Production Company and is currently dry.
The vicinity of these wells to the subject well's surface location made them ideal for generating a
well-rounded prognosis of formation tops. Other offset wells, including the Ward USA 34-
7TFH were also used for structure control during the curve landing and lateral (Figure 2).
ENGINEERING
The well was spud on November 11, 2014 by H&P's rig 386. The surface hole was drilled using
a 13 ½" rock bit and 5" drill pipe to a depth of 2,060' MD. A freshwater based drilling fluid was
used during this operation. The surface hole was then isolated using 9 " 36 # J-55 casing set to
2,047' MD. The hole was then cemented to the surface before drilling the remaining vertical
hole. Drilling continued on November 15th, 2014. Before drilling, freshwater was displaced by
invert diesel drilling fluid with mud weights fluctuating between 9.65-10.25 pounds per gallon.
Utilizing two 8 ¾" PDC (Varel and Smith) bits, the vertical hole was drilled to a kick-off point
(KOP) of 9,508' MD in 47.5 drilling hours. The curve build began on November 18, 2014. One
bottom-hole assembly (BHA), including an 8 ¾" PDC Security bit and 2.38° fixed NOV motor,
was used to build the curve. The curve was drilled to a total depth of 11,070' MD in 16.7
drilling hours. After completing the curve, 7" casing was set and cemented to 11,054' MD using
32# L-80. In preparation for the lateral portion of the well, invert diesel drilling fluid was
displaced with salt water drilling fluid. Mud weights in the lateral portion ranged from 9.5-10.45
pounds per gallon. One 6" PDC Smith bit and one Security bit were used along with two 1.40°
fixed mud motors. These two assemblies drilled to total depth in 60.6 drilling hours.
The Angela Ward USA 24-7H reached a total depth of 21,135' MD on November 27, 2014, at a
closure direction of 4.40° and a true vertical depth (TVD) of 10,375.87'. The bottom-hole
location is 11,147.66' north and 857.64' east of surface location or approximately 213.55' FNL &
1,972.64' FWL, NE NW Section 6, T146N, R92W (Figure 2).

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods
Geologic analysis was provided by three Sunburst Consulting well-site geologists. Gas levels
were monitored using a MSI digital gas detector and chromatograph as well as a Pason gas
detector. The chromatograph was interfaced with a Pason electronic data recorder. The Pason
relayed data such as measured depth, bit depth, and pump stroke information to the MController
gas monitoring software. MController returned gas in the form of total gas units (100 units = 1%
methane equivalent in air) to be logged and displayed across the drilling location. Multiple
component gases (methane, ethane, propane, and butane) and their concentrations were recorded
in parts per million. ¼" Poly-Flo ® tubing was used to direct gas into the chromatograph where
the data was then translated and lagged to the correct depth. Rig crews caught lagged samples in
30' intervals under the supervision of well-site geologists. Analysis and evaluation of gas and
drill cuttings began in the Kibbey Formation at 8,050' MD, and ended in the Middle Bakken at
21,135'. Cuttings were observed in wet (isopropyl alcohol) and dry conditions under a binocular
microscope.
Lithology
The Kibbey Formation (Big Snowy Gp.) consists of red-orange siltstone with some gray to red
interbedded silty sandstone. There is a very distinct layer of limestone, referred to as the "Kibbey
Lime", which was logged at 8,083' TVD (-5,840' MSL) and consists of light to medium gray
mudstone. There is a thin layer of anhydrite right above the limestone that marks the top of the
"Kibbey Lime" marker.
The Charles Formation (Madison Gp.) consists of limestone and a large amount of evaporates
including salt and anhydrite. The First Salt was logged at 8,232' TVD (-5,989' MSL) and the
Base Last Salt was logged at 8,683' (-6,440' MSL).
The Mission Canyon Formation (Madison Gp.) consists of light to dark gray-brown limestone
and was logged at 8,870' TVD (-6,627' MSL). Some areas contain algae laminations, fossil
fragments, and trace amounts of intercrystalline porosity with dead oil staining.
The Lodgepole Formation (Madison Gp.) is characterized by medium to dark gray argillaceous
limestone. The top was logged at 9,468' TVD (-7,225' MSL) and is marked by a transition from
limestone to argillaceous limestone. The "False Bakken" is a layer of shale near the bottom of
the Lodgepole Formation. It was logged at 10,291' TVD (-8,048' MSL). The "Scallion" is a
layer of limestone at the base of the formation and was logged at 10,301' TVD (-8,058' MSL).
The Bakken Formation (Devonian-Mississippian) is comprised of two layers of black shale
and a mixed clastic and carbonate middle and lowermost member. The Upper Bakken Shale
Member was logged at 10,312' TVD (-8,069' MSL). This member is recognized by its high
gamma counts, an increase in rate of penetration (ROP), elevated total gas units and distinct
black, carbonaceous and petroliferous shale (Figure 3). The Middle Bakken Member consists
of three distinct lithologies and was logged at 10,333' TVD (-8,090' MSL). A layer of siltstone
lies directly below the upper member, then resides a laterally discontinuous layer of fossiliferous
(packstone) limestone. Below the limestone facies, the target zone is comprised of gray to brown
silty sandstone, containing fine intergranular porosity and light brown, spotty oil staining
(Figure 4).
Figures 3 & 4. Wet cuttings of upper Bakken shale (left) and middle Bakken silty sandstone (right).
Geo-steering
The prognosis called for a landing target of 10,353' TVD, at an inclination of 90°. The prognosis
for the top of the target was 10,348' TVD and the bottom of the target was 10,358' TVD,
providing a 10' target window. The landing target was set 20' below the base of the upper
Bakken shale and 5' below the top of the target window. Using gamma-ray data, well-site
geologists were able to correlate formation tops, from the Angela Ward USA 24-7H, to nearby
offset wells in the area to assure an accurate landing. There were no changes made to the landing
target after the lower formation tops (L3000 through Bakken) came in with in 1' of the well
prognosis with the exception of the L4000, which came in 9' below the well prognosis. The well
landed 2' low to our target, at 10,355' TVD. This placed the well-bore 7' below the top of our
original target window.
Gamma-ray signatures in the target window were very consistent at 70-90 (API) gamma. The
only variation in this was an increase at the extreme, top of the target window to a larger
wavelength gamma of 90-105 (API). The other variation was 1-2' above the bottom of the target
window where a decrease to 50 (API) was observed.
The Middle Bakken target window was entered at approximately 10,953' MD (10,348' TVD).
The well-bore was maintained in the target zone for 85% of the lateral. The Middle Bakken
Member dropped 13.50' TVD over the course of the 10,256' lateral, resulting in a gross apparent
dip of -0.08° (Figure 5).

Gas and Oil Show
The label used to quantify gas for this well was units (100 units is equal to 1% methane
equivalent in air). The first time any significant gas was logged was a gas show of 43 units in the
Mission Canyon Formation, at a depth of 9,130' MD. Gas shows continued sporadically
throughout the remainder of the vertical portion of the well and varied in size from 10-50 units.
Background gas averaged 10 units in the vertical portion of the well until an increase to an
average of 20 units was observed at the start of the Lodgepole Formation. Gas shows increased
in size and abundance after the False Bakken marker was reached. The largest gas show
observed during the curve was 389 units in the upper member of the Bakken Formation, at a
depth of 10,835' MD.
During lateral operations, background gas varied from 101-3,444 units. Average background gas
for the lateral was ~2,500 units. Gas shows were common, with the largest registering 3,621
units at 11,824' MD. The largest connection gas peaked at 3,358 units, at 18,115' MD. Drill
fluid was circulated through the buster starting at 11,950' MD, and continued for the remainder
of the well. A flare was also observed from 11,950' MD, and continued through the remainer of
the well. The flare reached as high as 20' with 5' being the most common. Due to the high
amount of gas recorded, casing back-pressure was held, starting at 18,850' MD and continued
until total depth (Figure 6). Throughout parts of the lateral, light green to medium brown oil was
observed coming over the shakers and in sample.

SUMMARY
The Marathon Oil Company, Angela Ward USA 24-7H is a Middle Bakken lateral well. The
well spud on November 11, 2014, and was drilled to a kick off point of 9,508' MD. The curve
landed at 10,355' TVD. The Middle Bakken Member, target zone presented gray-brown silty
sandstone, containing fine intergranular porosity and light brown, spotty oil staining.
Background gas in the lateral ranged from 100-3,000 units, with gas shows as high as 3,621
units. Due to the high amount of gas, drill fluid was circulated through the gas buster from
11,950' MD to the end of the lateral. Flares as large as 20' were observed. The well-bore was
maintained within the target interval for 85% of the lateral section. The Angela Ward USA 24-
7H reached a total depth of 21,135' MD on November 27, 2014, after 16 drilling days.
Respectfully Submitted,
Samantha Buhr

Lithology
Angela Ward USA 24-7H
Lagged samples were caught by rig crews under the supervision of Sunburst geologists in 30' intervals from 8,050'
to 21,135' (TD). Drilling fluid was diesel invert in the vertical and curve sections and post-casing operations was
replaced with a brine solution for the lateral. All samples were caught within compliance of North Dakota state
regulations as well as the policies and procedures of Marathon Oil Company. Samples were examined wet and dry
using a binocular microscope. Dried cuttings were then boxed and sent to the state of North Dakota as well as the
Marathon Oil Company sample storage facility.
Drilling in the Kibbey Formation
8,050-8,080 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-medium gray, occasional tan, microcrystalline, friable-firm, earthy
texture, no visible porosity; common SILTSTONE: light red-brown, rare dark brown, trace cream-tan, friable-firm,
sandy in part, sub-blocky, earthy texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity
8,080-8,110 SILTSTONE: light red-brown, rare dark brown, trace cream-tan, friable-firm, sub-blocky, earthy
texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity; occasional LIMESTONE: as above
Kibbey "Lime"
8,085' MD/ 8,083' TVD (-5,840')
8,110-8,140 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-medium gray, occasional tan, microcrystalline, friable-firm, earthy
texture, no visible porosity; occasional ANHYDRITE: off white-milky, gray, soft, massive, amorphous texture;
occasional SILTSTONE: as above
8,140-8,170 SILTSTONE: light red-brown, rare dark brown, trace cream-tan, friable-firm, sub-blocky, earthy
texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity; occasional ANHYDRITE: off white-milky, gray, soft, massive,
amorphous texture
8,170-8,200 SILTSTONE: light red-brown, rare dark brown, trace cream-tan, friable-firm, sub-blocky, earthy
texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity; occasional ANHYDRITE: off white-milky, gray, soft, massive,
amorphous texture
8,200-8,230 SILTSTONE: light red-brown, rare dark brown, trace cream-tan, friable-firm, sub-blocky, earthy
texture, calcite cemented, no visible porosity; occasional ANHYDRITE: off white-milky, gray, soft, massive,
amorphous texture
Charles Formation (1st Salt)
8,240' MD/ 8,232' TVD (-5,989')
8,230-8,260 SALT: translucent, clear, hard, crystalline texture; rare LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown,
occasional tan, microcrystalline, friable-firm, earthy texture, no visible porosity; rare SANDSTONE: as above
8,260-8,290 SALT: translucent, clear, hard, crystalline texture; rare LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown,
occasional tan, microcrystalline, friable-firm, earthy texture, no visible porosity
8,290-8,320 SALT: translucent, clear, hard, crystalline texture
8,320-8,350 SALT: translucent, clear, hard, crystalline texture; rare LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown,
occasional tan, microcrystalline, friable-firm, earthy texture, no visible porosity
8,350-8,380 SALT: translucent, clear, hard, crystalline texture; rare LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown,
occasional tan, microcrystalline, friable-firm, earthy texture, no visible porosity
8,380-8,410 SALT: translucent, clear, hard, crystalline texture; rare LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown,
occasional tan, microcrystalline, friable-firm, earthy texture, no visible porosity
8,410-8,440 SALT: translucent, clear, hard, crystalline texture
8,440-8,470 SALT: translucent, clear, hard, crystalline texture; rare LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown,

RE:
HORIZONTAL WELL
ANGELA WARD USA 24-7H
LOT1 Section 18-146N-92W
Dunn County
Well File # 29029
Dear Natalie:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 23505, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within
the 1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sec 6&7T146N R92W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. Due to drainage adjacent to the well site, a dike is required surrounding the entire location.
MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Ashleigh Devenberg at 701-290-3277 prior to
location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing
point is: 971'N. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well
head is: 11161'N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Natalie Menge
August 1, 2014

Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division,
Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number,
drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m.
and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours
or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey
contractor shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion.
Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director
may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is
hereby granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing
on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well
records wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall
permit the Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or
controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to
have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time
upon request. The information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and
shall be available only to the Commission and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

Gas Capture Plan
Angela Ward USA 24-7H / Ward USA 24-7TFH / Del ana Ward USA 14-7H
Sec 18 T146N R92W
Field: Werner
Flowback Strategy
Anticipated First Production date
Anticipated first production date for the three wells site is January 2015. It is expected that it will be connected to a
gas sales pipeline at first production.
Multi-well startup
It is currently planned for two wells to be flowed back together and the third to flowback after this. The flowback
period is expected to last approximately 3-10 days for each well.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates
Average Gas rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 1,600 MSCFD.
Average Oil rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 2,400 bopd
